The percentages of nuclear poly(A) RNA accumulation observed in <italic>nab2 F73D</italic> cells were typical of multiple independent experiments.</p>

FIGURE 5.nab2 F73D mutant cells grow similarly to wild-type cells but display nuclear accumulation of poly(A) RNA.A, nab2 F73D cells are viable and grow similarly to wild-type NAB2 cells. NAB2Delta cells maintained by a NAB2 URA3 plasmid and containing NAB2, nab2 DeltaN, nab2 F72D, or nab2 F73D LEU2 test plasmids were grown to saturation, serially diluted in 10-fold dilutions, and spotted on control and 5-FOA plates. Cells were grown at 30 degreesC. B, growth curve analysis of nab2 F73D cells confirms that they grow similarly to wild-type NAB2 cells. NAB2Delta cells carrying only NAB2, nab2 F72D, or nab2 F73D plasmids were grown to saturation, diluted, and their optical density was measured at A600 for 40 h as described under "Experimental Procedures." C, nab2 F73D cells display nuclear accumulation of poly(A) RNA. NAB2Delta cells carrying only NAB2, nab2 DeltaN, nab2 F72D, or nab2 F73D plasmids were grown in liquid culture at 30 degreesC and poly(A) RNA (Poly(A)) was visualized by FISH using an oligo(dT) probe as described under "Experimental Procedures." Cells were stained with DAPI to visualize the position of the nucleus. Corresponding differential interference contrast (DIC) images are shown. FISH results were quantitated as described under "Experimental Procedures" to assess the mean percentage of cells with nuclear accumulation of poly(A) RNA within 10 fields of at least 195 cells each (indicated to the right of DIC images). Variation in the percentage of cells with nuclear poly(A) RNA in each field of cells from the mean was assessed by calculating the standard deviation: NAB2, 3.2 +/- 1.0%; nab2 F72D, 3.9 +/- 1.5%; and nab2 F73D, 8.2 +/- 2.0%. Thus, nab2 F73D cells exhibit a 2.5-fold increase in nuclear poly(A) RNA accumulation relative to NAB2 cells, whereas nab2 F72D cells show only a modest 1.2-fold increase. The percentages of nuclear poly(A) RNA accumulation observed in nab2 F73D cells were typical of multiple independent experiments.

###xml 901 908 889 896 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig5" ref-type="fig">Fig. 5<italic>C</italic></xref>
###xml 919 923 907 911 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nab2</italic>
###xml 929 930 913 914 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">N</italic>
###xml 1003 1005 987 989 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref36">36</xref>
To determine whether disruption of the Nab2/Mlp1 interaction impacts mRNA export, we next assessed whether nab2 F72D or nab2 F73D cells show nuclear accumulation of poly(A) RNA in vivo. We examined poly(A) RNA localization in wild-type NAB2, nab2 F72D, and nab2 F73D cells by FISH and then quantitated the percentage of cells with nuclear poly(A) RNA accumulation as described under "Experimental Procedures." As a control, we also examined poly(A) RNA localization in nab2 DeltaN cells, which show nuclear accumulation of poly(A) RNA (36). NAB2Delta cells expressing NAB2, nab2 DeltaN, F72D, or F73D were processed for FISH using an oligo(dT) probe to visualize bulk poly(A) RNA. The nab2 F73D cells show a 2.5-fold increase in nuclear accumulation of poly(A) RNA compared with wild-type cells, whereas nab2 F72D cells show accumulation of poly(A) RNA in the nucleus comparable with wild-type cells (Fig. 5C). Control nab2 DeltaN cells show significant nuclear accumulation of poly(A) RNA as expected (36). This result suggests that the Nab2/Mlp1 interaction facilitates but is not absolutely required for mRNA export.
###end p 51
###begin p 52
###xml 490 499 490 499 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nab2 F72D</italic>
###xml 503 512 503 512 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 538 545 538 545 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5</italic>
###xml 547 548 547 548 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref8">8</xref>
###xml 553 559 553 559 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">yra1&#8211;8</italic>
###xml 561 563 561 563 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref21">21</xref>
###xml 667 671 667 671 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">NAB2</italic>
###xml 677 684 673 680 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5</italic>
###xml 711 720 707 716 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">NAB2 URA3</italic>
###xml 756 766 752 762 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">NAB2, nab2</italic>
###xml 772 779 764 771 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">N, F72D</italic>
###xml 783 792 775 784 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">F73D LEU2</italic>
###xml 896 913 888 905 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 977 989 969 981 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 NAB2</italic>
###xml 1005 1022 997 1014 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 nab2 F72D</italic>
###xml 1052 1064 1044 1056 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 NAB2</italic>
###xml 1078 1079 1070 1071 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 1072 1079 1064 1071 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig6" ref-type="fig">Fig. 6<italic>A</italic></xref>
###xml 1143 1155 1135 1147 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 nab2</italic>
###xml 1161 1162 1149 1150 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">N</italic>
###xml 1227 1244 1215 1232 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 1263 1275 1251 1263 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 NAB2</italic>
###xml 1396 1397 1384 1385 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 1390 1397 1378 1385 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig6" ref-type="fig">Fig. 6<italic>B</italic></xref>
###xml 1421 1425 1409 1413 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">NAB2</italic>
###xml 1431 1437 1415 1421 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">yra1&#8211;8</italic>
###xml 1464 1473 1448 1457 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">NAB2 URA3</italic>
###xml 1509 1519 1493 1503 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">NAB2, nab2</italic>
###xml 1525 1532 1505 1512 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">N, F72D</italic>
###xml 1536 1545 1516 1525 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">F73D LEU2</italic>
###xml 1630 1646 1610 1626 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">yra1&#8211;8 nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 1710 1721 1690 1701 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">yra1&#8211;8 NAB2</italic>
###xml 1735 1736 1715 1716 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 1729 1736 1709 1716 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig6" ref-type="fig">Fig. 6<italic>A</italic></xref>
###xml 1747 1763 1727 1743 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">yra1&#8211;8 nab2 F72D</italic>
###xml 1793 1804 1773 1784 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">yra1&#8211;8 NAB2</italic>
###xml 1843 1852 1823 1832 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 1900 1918 1880 1898 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 and yra1&#8211;8</italic>
###xml 685 690 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 1438 1443 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 2063 2068 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
Because multiple mRNA export factors contribute to efficient mRNA export, we considered the possibility that the interaction between Nab2 and Mlp1 might contribute to a step in mRNA export that is not normally rate-limiting in a wild-type background. Thus, an effect on overall cellular function as assayed by cell growth might only be evident in a genetic background where additional steps in mRNA export are compromised or suboptimal. We therefore tested for genetic interactions between nab2 F72D or nab2 F73D and mRNA export mutants, mex67-5 (8) or yra1-8 (21), at the permissive growth temperature for these conditional mutants. Using the plasmid shuffle assay, NAB2Delta mex67-5 yeast cells harboring the NAB2 URA3 maintenance plasmid and containing NAB2, nab2 DeltaN, F72D or F73D LEU2 test plasmids were grown to saturation, serially diluted, and spotted on control and 5-FOA plates. The mex67-5 nab2 F73D double mutant cells show a slow growth phenotype compared with mex67-5 NAB2 cells, whereas mex67-5 nab2 F72D cells show growth similar to mex67-5 NAB2 cells (Fig. 6A). Further supporting a functional link between Mex67 and Nab2, mex67-5 nab2 DeltaN cells are not viable. We confirmed the slow growth phenotype of mex67-5 nab2 F73D cells relative to mex67-5 NAB2 cells by measuring the optical density of the cells in liquid cultures and generating quantitative growth curves (Fig. 6B). In a similar manner, NAB2Delta yra1-8 yeast cells harboring the NAB2 URA3 maintenance plasmid and containing NAB2, nab2 DeltaN, F72D or F73D LEU2 test plasmids were grown to saturation and spotted on control and 5-FOA plates. The yra1-8 nab2 F73D double mutant cells show a slow growth phenotype compared with yra1-8 NAB2 cells (Fig. 6A), whereas yra1-8 nab2 F72D cells show growth similar to yra1-8 NAB2 cells. These results demonstrate that nab2 F73D genetically interacts with mRNA export mutants mex67-5 and yra1-8 at their permissive temperatures. Together, the data suggest that although disrupting the Nab2 interaction with Mlp1 does not detectably impact yeast cell growth when the mRNA export pathway is fully functional, it does impact cell growth when mRNA export is suboptimal.
###end p 52

FISH results were quantitated as described under "Experimental Procedures" to assess the mean percentage of cells with nuclear accumulation of poly(A) RNA within 10 fields of at least 43 cells each (indicated to the right of the DIC images). Variation in the percentage of cells with nuclear poly(A) RNA in each field of cells from the mean was assessed by calculating the standard deviation: mex67-5 NAB2, 18.6 +/- 4.8%; mex67-5 nab2 F72D, 20.3 +/- 6.0%; and mex67-5 nab2 F73D, 30.8 +/- 6.9. Thus, mex67-5 nab2 F73D cells exhibit a 1.7-fold increase in nuclear poly(A) RNA accumulation relative to mex67-5 NAB2 cells, whereas mex67-5 nab2 F72D cells show only a slight 1.1-fold increase. The percentages of nuclear poly(A) RNA accumulation observed in mex67-5 nab2 F73D cells were typical of multiple independent experiments.
###end p 53
###begin p 54
###xml 4 116 4 116 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nab2 F73D mutant displays genetic interactions with mRNA export mutants mex67-5 and yra1&#8211;8 and mex67-5 nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 0 161 0 161 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">The <italic>nab2 F73D mutant displays genetic interactions with mRNA export mutants mex67-5 and yra1&#8211;8 and mex67-5 nab2 F73D</italic> cells show nuclear poly(A) RNA accumulation.</bold>
###xml 161 181 161 181 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A, mex67-5 nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 191 207 191 207 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">yra1&#8211;8 nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 244 248 244 248 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">NAB2</italic>
###xml 254 261 250 257 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5</italic>
###xml 265 269 261 265 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">NAB2</italic>
###xml 275 281 267 273 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">yra1&#8211;8</italic>
###xml 304 313 296 305 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">NAB2 URA3</italic>
###xml 337 347 329 339 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">NAB2, nab2</italic>
###xml 353 365 341 353 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">N, nab2 F72D</italic>
###xml 370 384 358 372 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nab2 F73D LEU2</italic>
###xml 537 538 519 520 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 565 582 547 564 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 630 642 612 624 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 NAB2</italic>
###xml 650 662 632 644 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 NAB2</italic>
###xml 688 703 666 681 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">NAB2, nab2 F72D</italic>
###xml 708 717 686 695 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 804 805 782 783 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 805 808 783 786 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">600</sub>
###xml 864 884 842 862 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C, mex67-5 nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 933 937 911 915 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">NAB2</italic>
###xml 943 950 917 924 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5</italic>
###xml 971 986 945 960 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">NAB2, nab2 F72D</italic>
###xml 991 1000 965 974 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 1071 1075 1039 1043 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Poly</italic>
###xml 1076 1077 1044 1045 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 1295 1298 1263 1266 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">DIC</italic>
###xml 1534 1539 1502 1507 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">right</italic>
###xml 1711 1723 1679 1691 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 NAB2</italic>
###xml 1740 1757 1706 1723 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 nab2 F72D</italic>
###xml 1778 1795 1742 1759 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 1817 1834 1779 1796 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 1917 1929 1879 1891 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 NAB2</italic>
###xml 1945 1962 1907 1924 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 nab2 F72D</italic>
###xml 2071 2088 2033 2050 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 nab2 F73D</italic>
The nab2 F73D mutant displays genetic interactions with mRNA export mutants mex67-5 and yra1-8 and mex67-5 nab2 F73D cells show nuclear poly(A) RNA accumulation.A, mex67-5 nab2 F73D cells or yra1-8 nab2 F73D cells have a slow growth phenotype. NAB2Delta mex67-5 or NAB2Delta yra1-8 cells maintained by a NAB2 URA3 plasmid and containing NAB2, nab2 DeltaN, nab2 F72D, or nab2 F73D LEU2 test plasmids were grown to saturation, serially diluted in 10-fold dilutions and spotted on control and 5-FOA plates. Cells were grown at 30 degreesC. B, growth curve analysis of mex67-5 nab2 F73D cells confirms that they grow more slowly than mex67-5 NAB2 cells. mex67-5 NAB2Delta cells carrying only NAB2, nab2 F72D, or nab2 F73D plasmids were grown to saturation, diluted, and their optical density was measured at A600 for 40 h as described under "Experimental Procedures." C, mex67-5 nab2 F73D cells show nuclear accumulation of poly(A) RNA. NAB2Delta mex67-5 cells carrying only NAB2, nab2 F72D, or nab2 F73D plasmids were grown in liquid culture at 30 degreesC and poly(A) RNA (Poly(A)) was visualized by FISH using an oligo(dT) probe as described under "Experimental Procedures." Cells were stained with DAPI to visualize the position of the nucleus. Corresponding differential interference contrast (DIC) images are shown. FISH results were quantitated as described under "Experimental Procedures" to assess the mean percentage of cells with nuclear accumulation of poly(A) RNA within 10 fields of at least 43 cells each (indicated to the right of the DIC images). Variation in the percentage of cells with nuclear poly(A) RNA in each field of cells from the mean was assessed by calculating the standard deviation: mex67-5 NAB2, 18.6 +/- 4.8%; mex67-5 nab2 F72D, 20.3 +/- 6.0%; and mex67-5 nab2 F73D, 30.8 +/- 6.9. Thus, mex67-5 nab2 F73D cells exhibit a 1.7-fold increase in nuclear poly(A) RNA accumulation relative to mex67-5 NAB2 cells, whereas mex67-5 nab2 F72D cells show only a slight 1.1-fold increase. The percentages of nuclear poly(A) RNA accumulation observed in mex67-5 nab2 F73D cells were typical of multiple independent experiments.
###end p 54
###begin p 55
###xml 15 24 15 24 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 151 158 151 158 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5</italic>
###xml 362 379 362 379 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 551 558 545 552 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5</italic>
###xml 615 616 609 610 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref8">8</xref>
###xml 619 623 613 617 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">NAB2</italic>
###xml 629 636 619 626 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5</italic>
###xml 654 669 644 659 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">NAB2, nab2 F72D</italic>
###xml 674 683 664 673 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 767 784 757 774 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 869 881 859 871 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 NAB2</italic>
###xml 895 896 885 886 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C</italic>
###xml 889 896 879 886 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig6" ref-type="fig">Fig. 6<italic>C</italic></xref>
###xml 1006 1013 996 1003 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">in vivo</italic>
Given that the nab2 F73D cells showed a mild mRNA export defect in a wild-type background, we wished to assess whether cells expressing Nab2 F73D in a mex67-5 mRNA export mutant background, which showed a severe cell growth defect, exhibit a similar or more pronounced mRNA export defect. To address this possibility, we examined poly(A) RNA localization in the mex67-5 nab2 F73D cells and quantitated the percentage of cells with nuclear poly(A) RNA accumulation. Importantly, we examined the cells at the permissive temperature of 30 degreesC where mex67-5 cells show minimal nuclear accumulation of poly(A) RNA (8). NAB2Delta mex67-5 cells expressing NAB2, nab2 F72D, or nab2 F73D were processed for FISH with an oligo(dT) probe to visualize bulk poly(A) RNA. The mex67-5 nab2 F73D cells show a 1.7-fold increase in nuclear accumulation of poly(A) RNA compared with mex67-5 NAB2 cells (Fig. 6C). The combined results suggest that Nab2-F73D, which disrupts the Nab2/Mlp1 interaction, impacts mRNA export in vivo.
###end p 55
###begin title 56
DISCUSSION
###end title 56
###begin p 57
###xml 321 328 321 328 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">in vivo</italic>
###xml 390 399 390 399 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 476 481 476 481 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">MEX67</italic>
###xml 486 490 486 490 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">YRA1</italic>
###xml 1071 1073 1071 1073 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref59">59</xref>
###xml 1075 1077 1075 1077 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref60">60</xref>
In this study, we have examined the functional significance of the interaction between the poly(A) RNA-binding protein, Nab2, and the nuclear pore-associated protein, Mlp1, to test a model where Nab2 facilitates targeting of mRNA for export via interaction with Mlp1. We find that disruption of the Nab2/Mlp1 interaction in vivo causes nuclear accumulation of poly(A) RNA. Furthermore, the nab2 F73D mutant shows genetic interactions with two genes essential for mRNA export, MEX67 and YRA1, supporting the hypothesis that Nab2 binding to Mlp1 contributes to efficient mRNA export. In addition, we have characterized the Nab2/Mlp1 interaction in detail and find that the Nab2-binding domain of Mlp1 (Mlp1-NBD) is sufficient to bind to the N-terminal domain of Nab2 (Nab2-N) and cause nuclear accumulation of poly(A) RNA, suggesting that Nab2 is an important molecular link between Mlp1 and poly(A) RNA. We also find that Mlp1-NBD binds to Nab2-N with micromolar affinity, indicating that the Nab2/Mlp1 interaction, like other mRNA export factor-nucleoporin interactions (59, 60), is comparatively weak. Together, the results are consistent with the notion that Nab2 facilitates targeting of mRNA for export via transient interaction with Mlp1 and acts in concert with other mRNA export factors to coordinate proper mRNA export.
###end p 57
###begin p 58
###xml 322 324 318 320 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref61">61</xref>
###xml 400 413 396 409 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Saccharomyces</italic>
###xml 883 885 875 877 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">73</sup>
We have mapped the Nab2-binding domain of Mlp1 (Mlp1-NBD) to a 183-amino acid region (residues 1586-1768) within CT-Mlp1. Analysis of the Mlp1-NBD protein sequence using Phyre () suggests that it forms a predominantly alpha-helical secondary structure, with the initial 90 residues (1586-1676) likely to form two helices (61). Sequence alignment of the Mlp1-NBD peptide with Mlp1 peptides from other Saccharomyces species highlights key hydrophobic residues within the first 90 residues of Mlp1-NBD that have been evolutionarily conserved and perhaps retained because they form alpha-helical secondary structure or serve as functional contact sites. It will be necessary to determine the structure of Mlp1-NBD and its complex with Nab2-N to define the Mlp1-NBD fold more precisely and identify the residues within Mlp1-NBD that make contact with the hydrophobic patch and residue Phe73 in Nab2-N.
###end p 58
###begin p 59
###xml 158 159 158 159 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">d</sub>
###xml 157 159 157 159 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">K<sub>d</sub></italic>
###xml 180 181 167 168 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 394 396 381 383 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref59">59</xref>
###xml 398 400 385 387 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref60">60</xref>
###xml 471 472 458 459 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">d</sub>
###xml 470 472 457 459 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">K<sub>d</sub></italic>
###xml 482 483 468 469 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 546 547 532 533 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">d</sub>
###xml 545 547 531 533 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">K<sub>d</sub></italic>
###xml 558 559 543 544 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 561 563 546 548 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref59">59</xref>
###xml 565 567 550 552 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref60">60</xref>
###xml 611 612 595 596 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 894 901 878 885 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">in vivo</italic>
Analysis of the binding between Nab2-N and Mlp1-NBD indicates that Mlp1-NBD binds to Nab2-N with a relatively weak affinity that is in the micromolar range (Kd approximately 1.3 mum). Apparent binding affinities between the nuclear transport factor, NTF2, or the mRNA receptor heterodimer, TAP-p15, and FG repeat-containing nucleoporins have been measured and are also in the micromolar range (59, 60). For example, NTF2 binds to FG repeat nucleoporins with an apparent Kd of 1-4 mum and TAP-p15 binds to FG repeat nucleoporins with an apparent Kd of 4-11 mum (59, 60). Therefore, the binding constant of 1.3 mum observed between Nab2 and Mlp1 is comparable with the binding constants measured between other nuclear transport factors and FG-nucleoporins. Like the low-affinity transport factor-nucleoporin interactions, the rather weak Nab2/Mlp1 interaction is therefore likely to be transient in vivo. In this way, Nab2 may bind transiently to Mlp1 with a relatively high off-rate consistent with rapid transport of the properly assembled mRNA export complex.
###end p 59
###begin p 60
###xml 230 238 230 238 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">in vitro</italic>
###xml 273 275 273 275 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">73</sup>
###xml 430 431 430 431 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">d</sub>
###xml 429 431 429 431 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">K<sub>d</sub></italic>
###xml 452 453 439 440 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 489 490 476 477 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">d</sub>
###xml 488 490 475 477 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">K<sub>d</sub></italic>
###xml 511 512 485 486 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
Quantitative analysis of the interaction between Nab2-N-F73D and Mlp1-NBD shows that Mlp1-NBD binding to Nab2-N-F73D is too weak to measure. This result supports previous data showing that CT-Mlp1 cannot interact with Nab2-N-F73D in vitro and confirms that Nab2 residue Phe73 is critical for the Nab2/Mlp1 interaction. In addition, we find that Mlp1-NBD binds to a second Nab2 mutant, Nab2-N-F73W, with 1.5-fold higher affinity (Kd approximately 0.8 mum) compared with wild-type protein (Kd approximately 1.3 mum). This result strengthens the idea that large hydrophobic residues within Nab2-N are important for binding to Mlp1 and underscores the hydrophobic nature of the Nab2/Mlp1 interaction.
###end p 60
###begin p 61
###xml 119 126 119 126 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">in vivo</italic>
###xml 184 193 184 193 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 284 289 284 289 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">MEX67</italic>
###xml 294 298 294 298 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">YRA1</italic>
###xml 411 420 411 420 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 513 517 513 517 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">NAB2</italic>
###xml 867 884 867 884 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 977 989 977 989 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 NAB2</italic>
###xml 1093 1110 1093 1110 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 1409 1426 1409 1426 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 1651 1668 1639 1656 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nab2 F73D mex67-5</italic>
###xml 1834 1843 1810 1819 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nab2 F73D</italic>
A key finding of this study is that expression of Nab2 F73D and the consequent disruption of the Nab2/Mlp1 interaction in vivo causes nuclear accumulation of poly(A) RNA and that this nab2 F73D mutant displays genetic interactions with alleles of two genes essential for mRNA export, MEX67 and YRA1. This result indicates that the Nab2/Mlp1 interaction is functionally important and contributes to mRNA export. nab2 F73D cells show a 2.5-fold increase in nuclear accumulation of poly(A) RNA relative to wild-type NAB2 cells, but do not exhibit a detectable growth defect. A potential explanation for this result is that the Nab2/Mlp1 interaction increases the rate and/or efficiency of one step of the mRNA export pathway that is not normally rate-limiting and therefore the Nab2/Mlp1 interaction is not absolutely required for cell growth in a wild-type background. mex67-5 nab2 F73D cells, however, show a 1.7-fold increase in nuclear accumulation of poly(A) RNA relative to mex67-5 NAB2 cells and clearly exhibit a decrease in cell growth. One possible explanation for the growth defect in mex67-5 nab2 F73D cells is that the Nab2/Mlp1 interaction becomes critical for a cellular function, such as efficient mRNA export, when additional steps in mRNA export and/or mRNA metabolism are compromised due to impairment of the Mex67 mRNA export receptor. A second potential explanation for the growth defect in mex67-5 nab2 F73D cells is that a threshold number of cells that exhibit mRNA export defects within the population must be reached before any effects on the overall growth properties of the culture are observed. Thus, the approximately30% of nab2 F73D mex67-5 cells that show nuclear accumulation of poly(A) RNA may be sufficient to impact the overall growth properties of the cell population, whereas the approximately8% of nab2 F73D cells that show nuclear poly(A) RNA accumulation may not be sufficient. Further study will be required to ascertain precisely how defects in cell growth are linked to impaired mRNA export.
###end p 61
###begin p 62
###xml 233 234 233 234 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 227 234 227 234 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig7" ref-type="fig">Fig. 7<italic>A</italic></xref>
###xml 335 337 335 337 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref21">21</xref>
###xml 339 341 339 341 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref62">62</xref>
###xml 442 444 442 444 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref34">34</xref>
###xml 445 447 445 447 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref36">36</xref>
###xml 496 498 496 498 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref18">18</xref>
###xml 500 502 500 502 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref19">19</xref>
###xml 569 571 569 571 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref16">16</xref>
###xml 675 677 675 677 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
###xml 738 740 738 740 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref38">38</xref>
###xml 1090 1092 1090 1092 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
###xml 1094 1096 1094 1096 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref63">63</xref>
###xml 1219 1221 1219 1221 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref64">64</xref>
###xml 1223 1225 1223 1225 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref65">65</xref>
###xml 1286 1288 1286 1288 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref66">66</xref>
###xml 1289 1291 1289 1291 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref69">69</xref>
###xml 1367 1369 1367 1369 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref70">70</xref>
###xml 1422 1424 1422 1424 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref71">71</xref>
###xml 1571 1573 1571 1573 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref70">70</xref>
###xml 1575 1577 1575 1577 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref71">71</xref>
The analysis of the Nab2 F73D mutant presented here and previous work on components of the mRNA export pathway suggest a model for Nab2 function in mRNA export in which Nab2 helps to target mRNA to the nuclear pore for export (Fig. 7A). In this simplified model, mRNA is co-transcriptionally loaded with the mRNA export adaptor, Yra1 (21, 62), and the poly(A) tails of the mRNA are specifically bound by Nab2 during or after polyadenylation (34-36). Yra1 binds to the mRNA export protein, Mex67 (18, 19), and recruits the Mex67/Mtr2 heterodimeric receptor to the mRNA (16). Mex67/Mtr2 then interacts with FG-nucleoporins at the pore to translocate the mRNA to the cytoplasm (17). Alongside Yra1 and Mex67, Nab2 binds to Mlp1 at the pore (38), via interaction between the Nab2-N hydrophobic patch and the Mlp1-NBD, to help concentrate the mRNA at the pore for interaction with other mRNA export factors and transport to the cytoplasm. The assembled mRNA complex containing Nab2 is then translocated through the NPC channel by Mex67/Mtr2, which interacts with FG-nucleoporins in the channel (17, 63). Upon reaching the cytoplasmic face of the nuclear pore, the mRNA export complex encounters the DEAD-box helicase, Dbp5 (64, 65), which is bound to and activated by the nucleoporin, Gle1 (66-69), and Dbp5 remodels the mRNP to trigger dissociation of Nab2 from the RNA (70), release of Mex67, and disassembly of the complex (71). Importantly, examination of Dbp5 function suggests that disassembly of the mRNA export complex is probably a rate-limiting step in mRNA export (70, 71). In a more detailed mRNA export model, several other mRNA export adaptors, hnRNPs, and mRNA processing factors can be added that aid in the concentration of mRNA at the nuclear face of the pore, the translocation of that mRNA through the pore and its remodeling and disassembly at the cytoplasmic face of the pore.
###end p 62
###begin p 63
###xml 0 9 0 9 <label xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FIGURE 7.</label>
###xml 100 117 100 117 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 9 154 9 154 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Models for Nab2 function in mRNA export and the observed growth and mRNA export defects in <italic>mex67-5 nab2 F73D</italic> cells at the permissive temperature.</bold>
###xml 154 155 154 155 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 346 348 346 348 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref21">21</xref>

###xml 9 2013 9 2013 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" textid="64"><bold>Models for Nab2 function in mRNA export and the observed growth and mRNA export defects in <italic>mex67-5 nab2 F73D</italic> cells at the permissive temperature.</bold><italic>A</italic>, model for Nab2 function in mRNA export in which Nab2 helps to target mRNA to the nuclear pore for export. Initially, mRNA is co-transcriptionally loaded with the mRNA export adaptor, Yra1 (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="ref21">21</xref>, <xref ref-type="bibr" rid="ref62">62</xref>), and bound by Nab2 at the poly(A) tail (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="ref34">34</xref>&#8211;<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="ref36">36</xref>). Yra1 then binds to the mRNA export protein, Mex67 (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="ref18">18</xref>, <xref ref-type="bibr" rid="ref19">19</xref>), recruiting the Mex67/Mtr2 heterodimeric receptor to the mRNA (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="ref16">16</xref>) and Mex67/Mtr2 interacts with FG-nucleoporins at the pore to translocate the mRNA to the cytoplasm (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>). Alongside Yra1 and Mex67, Nab2 binds to Mlp1 at the pore (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="ref38">38</xref>), via the Nab2-N/Mlp1-NBD interaction. Upon reaching the cytoplasmic face of the nuclear pore, the mRNA export complex encounters the DEAD-box helicase, Dbp5 (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="ref64">64</xref>, <xref ref-type="bibr" rid="ref65">65</xref>), tethered and activated by the nucleoporin, Gle1 (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="ref66">66</xref>&#8211;<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="ref69">69</xref>), which remodels the mRNP to trigger dissociation of Nab2 from the RNA (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="ref70">70</xref>), release of Mex67, and disassembly of the complex (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="ref71">71</xref>). <italic>B</italic>, model to explain the observed growth and mRNA export defects in <italic>mex67-5 nab2 F73D</italic> cells at the permissive temperature in which combined impairment of Mex67 and Nab2 reduces mRNA export. Here, the Mex67-5 mutant, which cannot interact with Mtr2 and FG-nucleoporins at the non-permissive temperature (<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="ref8">8</xref>, <xref ref-type="bibr" rid="ref16">16</xref>), may also be impaired in binding to FG-nucleoporins at the permissive temperature, potentially resulting in a moderate reduction in the rate of translocation. Similarly, the Nab2 F73D mutant, which cannot interact with Mlp1, may reduce the rate of mRNA concentration at the pore. Combination of the reduction in mRNA translocation rate produced by Mex67-5 and reduction in the mRNA concentration rate caused by Nab2 F73D could become rate-limiting and result in a decreased rate of mRNA export coupled with nuclear accumulation of poly(A) RNA.</p>

###begin p 64
###xml 91 108 91 108 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 0 145 0 145 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Models for Nab2 function in mRNA export and the observed growth and mRNA export defects in <italic>mex67-5 nab2 F73D</italic> cells at the permissive temperature.</bold>
###xml 145 146 145 146 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 337 339 337 339 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref21">21</xref>
###xml 341 343 341 343 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref62">62</xref>
###xml 385 387 385 387 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref34">34</xref>
###xml 388 390 388 390 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref36">36</xref>
###xml 444 446 444 446 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref18">18</xref>
###xml 448 450 448 450 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref19">19</xref>
###xml 515 517 515 517 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref16">16</xref>
###xml 619 621 619 621 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
###xml 682 684 682 684 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref38">38</xref>
###xml 827 829 827 829 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
###xml 831 833 831 833 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref63">63</xref>
###xml 956 958 956 958 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref64">64</xref>
###xml 960 962 960 962 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref65">65</xref>
###xml 1014 1016 1014 1016 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref66">66</xref>
###xml 1017 1019 1017 1019 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref69">69</xref>
###xml 1092 1094 1092 1094 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref70">70</xref>
###xml 1147 1149 1147 1149 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref71">71</xref>
###xml 1152 1153 1152 1153 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 1219 1236 1219 1236 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 1454 1455 1454 1455 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref8">8</xref>
###xml 1457 1459 1457 1459 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref16">16</xref>
Models for Nab2 function in mRNA export and the observed growth and mRNA export defects in mex67-5 nab2 F73D cells at the permissive temperature.A, model for Nab2 function in mRNA export in which Nab2 helps to target mRNA to the nuclear pore for export. Initially, mRNA is co-transcriptionally loaded with the mRNA export adaptor, Yra1 (21, 62), and bound by Nab2 at the poly(A) tail (34-36). Yra1 then binds to the mRNA export protein, Mex67 (18, 19), recruiting the Mex67/Mtr2 heterodimeric receptor to the mRNA (16) and Mex67/Mtr2 interacts with FG-nucleoporins at the pore to translocate the mRNA to the cytoplasm (17). Alongside Yra1 and Mex67, Nab2 binds to Mlp1 at the pore (38), via the Nab2-N/Mlp1-NBD interaction. The assembled mRNA complex containing Nab2 is then translocated through the NPC channel by Mex67/Mtr2 (17, 63). Upon reaching the cytoplasmic face of the nuclear pore, the mRNA export complex encounters the DEAD-box helicase, Dbp5 (64, 65), tethered and activated by the nucleoporin, Gle1 (66-69), which remodels the mRNP to trigger dissociation of Nab2 from the RNA (70), release of Mex67, and disassembly of the complex (71). B, model to explain the observed growth and mRNA export defects in mex67-5 nab2 F73D cells at the permissive temperature in which combined impairment of Mex67 and Nab2 reduces mRNA export. Here, the Mex67-5 mutant, which cannot interact with Mtr2 and FG-nucleoporins at the non-permissive temperature (8, 16), may also be impaired in binding to FG-nucleoporins at the permissive temperature, potentially resulting in a moderate reduction in the rate of translocation. Similarly, the Nab2 F73D mutant, which cannot interact with Mlp1, may reduce the rate of mRNA concentration at the pore. Combination of the reduction in mRNA translocation rate produced by Mex67-5 and reduction in the mRNA concentration rate caused by Nab2 F73D could become rate-limiting and result in a decreased rate of mRNA export coupled with nuclear accumulation of poly(A) RNA.
###end p 64
###begin p 65
###xml 6 7 6 7 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 0 7 0 7 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig7" ref-type="fig">Fig. 7<italic>B</italic></xref>
###xml 97 114 97 114 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 246 247 246 247 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref8">8</xref>
###xml 249 251 249 251 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref16">16</xref>
###xml 454 456 454 456 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
###xml 1295 1312 1295 1312 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 1600 1617 1600 1617 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 nab2 F73D</italic>
Fig. 7B presents a plausible model to account for the observed growth and mRNA export defects in mex67-5 nab2 F73D cells. We envisage that the Mex67-5 mutant, which cannot interact with Mtr2 and FG-nucleoporins at the non-permissive temperature (8, 16), may also be impaired in binding to FG-nucleoporins even at the permissive temperature. As the interaction between Mex67 and the FG-nucleoporins is necessary for the translocation step of mRNA export (17), the Mex67-5 mutant may reduce the rate of translocation through the nuclear pore. At the permissive temperature, this modest reduction in the rate of translocation produced by Mex67-5 may not impact the overall rate of mRNA export as the translocation step is probably not normally rate-limiting. Similarly, the Nab2 F73D mutant, which cannot interact with Mlp1, may reduce the rate of mRNA concentration at the pore. At the permissive temperature, this moderate reduction in the rate of mRNA concentration produced by Nab2 F73D may not affect the total rate of mRNA export as the concentration step is also probably not normally rate-limiting. However, the cumulative effect of impairing both mRNA translocation and concentration steps could be more marked and reduce the overall rate of mRNA export. At the permissive temperature, in mex67-5 nab2 F73D cells, the combined reduction in the mRNA translocation rate produced by Mex67-5 and the reduction in mRNA concentration rate caused by Nab2 F73D could become rate-limiting and result in a decreased rate of mRNA export coupled with nuclear accumulation of poly(A) RNA. Alternatively, in mex67-5 nab2 F73D cells, malformed mRNP complexes containing Nab2 F73D and Mex67-5 may be generated that are not recognized and removed by the surveillance machinery because Nab2 F73D does not bind to Mlp1 efficiently. Further work will be required to distinguish between these alternative models.
###end p 65
###begin p 66
###xml 87 94 87 94 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">in vivo</italic>
###xml 358 367 358 367 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 402 419 402 419 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">mex67-5 nab2 F73D</italic>
###xml 303 308 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
The combined data presented here highlight the importance of the Nab2/Mlp1 interaction in vivo and underscore the extent of cooperation between mRNA export factors, Nab2, Yra1, and Mex67, that is necessary for efficient mRNA export. In addition, the data suggest that although the mRNA export system in yeast can tolerate single component mutations, such as nab2 F73D, double component mutations, like mex67-5 nab2 F73D, produce a growth defect and significant nuclear accumulation of poly(A) RNA, consistent with the step in the export pathway in which they participate becoming rate-limiting, even under permissive conditions. The results of this study are therefore consistent with a model in which Nab2 helps to target the mRNP complex to the nuclear pore via interaction with Mlp1 to facilitate mRNA export. In this model, it is clear that Nab2 acts in concert with other mRNA export factors, particularly Yra1 and Mex67, to form an mRNP that is competent of export. Future studies on the genetic and physical interactions between Nab2 and other mRNA export components will help to elucidate the underlying mechanism of mRNA export in eukaryotic organisms.
###end p 66

###xml 372 373 372 373 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S</italic>

The abbreviations used are: hnRNP, heterogeneous nuclear ribonucleoprotein; NPC, nuclear pore complex; FG-nucleoporin, phenylalanine-glycine repeat-containing nuclear pore protein; Mlp1, myosin-like protein 1; CT-Mlp1, C-terminal domain of Mlp1; Nab2-N, N-terminal domain of Nab2; Mlp1-NBD, Nab2-binding domain of Mlp1; Tpr, translocated promoter region; GST, glutathione S-transferase; PBS, phosphate-buffered saline; BSA, bovine serum albumin; GFP, green fluorescent protein; DAPI, 4',6-diamidino-2-phenylindole-dihydrochloride; 5-FOA, 5-fluoroorotic acid; FISH, fluorescence in situ hybridization; DTT, dithiothreitol.
